  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_462688a6-4823-49e5-b2b1-e9e0d264ee3e'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer5852340703138634979">Do you want to be popular? Everyone wants to be popular or at least, Stephanie Landry does. Steph's been the least popular girl in her class since a certain cherry Super Big Gulp catastrophe five years earlier. Does being popular matter? It matters very much to Steph. That's why this year, she has a plan to get in with the It Crowd in no time flat. She's got a secret weapo</span>
  <span id="freeText5852340703138634979" style="display:none">Do you want to be popular? Everyone wants to be popular or at least, Stephanie Landry does. Steph's been the least popular girl in her class since a certain cherry Super Big Gulp catastrophe five years earlier. Does being popular matter? It matters very much to Steph. That's why this year, she has a plan to get in with the It Crowd in no time flat. She's got a secret weapon: an old book called what else? How to Be Popular. What does it take to be popular? All Steph has to do is follow the instructions in The Book, and soon she'll be partying with the It Crowd (including school quarterback Mark Finley) instead of sitting on The Hill Saturday nights, stargazing with her nerdy best pal Becca, and even nerdier Jason (now kind of hot, but still), whose passion for astronomy Steph once shared. Who needs red dwarves when you're invited to the hottest parties in town? But don't forget the most important thing about popularity! It's easy to become popular. What isn't so easy? Staying that way.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11204418065268165775">Read more bookish goodness on my book blog: <a href='https://thehyperlapse.blogspot.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cal's YA Reads</a><br/><br/>5/5 freaking dang stars. <br/><br/>I'm not going to write a full-blown review for this. <br/><br/>Here's the run down: <br/><br/>- I read this when I was 11/12. <br/>- I got it for my birthday and my friend who gave it to me said "my mum thought of you and thought it would be good for you" you GUYZZZZ I didn't EVER want to touch this book. <br/><br/>This impacted me greatly during the incoming high school years-- I feel like I was more level headed about the fascination of popularit</span>
  <span id="freeText11204418065268165775" style="display:none">Read more bookish goodness on my book blog: <a href="https://thehyperlapse.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cal's YA Reads</a><br /><br />5/5 freaking dang stars. <br /><br />I'm not going to write a full-blown review for this. <br /><br />Here's the run down: <br /><br />- I read this when I was 11/12. <br />- I got it for my birthday and my friend who gave it to me said "my mum thought of you and thought it would be good for you" you GUYZZZZ I didn't EVER want to touch this book. <br /><br />This impacted me greatly during the incoming high school years-- I feel like I was more level headed about the fascination of popularity. <br /><br />Why you should read this book:<br />- need chick lit but for a younger audience than most chick lit books<br />- need a bit of sarcasm and quirkiness <br />- need a bit of awkwardness like Bridget Jones who had a bit of pervy habits <br />- needed a cliche, happy ending (which is still the bomb) <br /><br />This book is my fave and I hold it dearly to my heart. I kind of hoped for this experience in high school but lol nope I'm now in uni and realise I completely didn't meet my 12 year old expectations…<br /><br />IM A SLUT FOR MEG CABOT'S BOOKS AND I CAN SEE THAT WILL NEVER CHANGE, NO MATTER WHAT DECADE IT IS.</span>

<div id="review_21682454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21682454" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21682454?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-personally-by-moi">read-personally-by-moi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21682454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4724800627174710449">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>If you've ever heard the phrase "Way to pull a Steph Landry!," you wouldn't be alone. Pretty much everyone who attends Bloomville High in the heart of Greene County, Indiana, knows who Steph Landry is. Or, they at least know better than to ever, ever, ever do something that would have someone uttering the aforementioned phrase. Even kids under the age of five know what it means to "pull a Steph Landry." In that they know it means instant social doom. <br/><br/>So what di</span>
  <span id="freeText4724800627174710449" style="display:none">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />If you've ever heard the phrase "Way to pull a Steph Landry!," you wouldn't be alone. Pretty much everyone who attends Bloomville High in the heart of Greene County, Indiana, knows who Steph Landry is. Or, they at least know better than to ever, ever, ever do something that would have someone uttering the aforementioned phrase. Even kids under the age of five know what it means to "pull a Steph Landry." In that they know it means instant social doom. <br /><br />So what did this girl do, you ask? Shoot someone? Rob a store? Dump the Homecoming Queen into a lake, lock the quarterback in a dungeon, lob a hand grenade into the general store? No, what Steph Landy did was much, much worse. She accidentally spilled a Big Red Super Big Gulp on Lauren Moffat's white D&amp;G skirt. And even though they had been kind of friends up until that incident in sixth grade, and even though her father tried to remove the stain from Lauren's skirt, and even though her mother ended up buying her a new one, and even though Steph herself apologized for the incident like ten zillion times, Lauren Moffat has been making Steph pay for her mistake ever since. <br /><br />They're all juniors in high school now--Steph and her best friends Jason and Becca, Lauren and her posse of popular girls and guys, most noticeably her football quarterback boyfriend, Mark Finley. Nearly five years after that accidental dousing in the middle school cafeteria, and Steph is still living down the horror of being a social outcast. <br /><br />That's all about to change, though. At least if she has anything to say about it. Now that Jason's grandmother is marrying her own widowed grandfather, they've been spending a lot of time at Jason's house. It's during one of those times that Steph finds the book; the one that will shoot her to the top of the popularity totem pole, the one that will exile the social pariah Steph once and for all, and turn her into mega-popular, wonderful, everyone loves her Steph. <br /><br />Kind of. Maybe. If she plays her cards right. Or she just might end up getting what she wants (popularity), and losing everything she's ever held dear (most noticeably, Jason). <br /><br />With HOW TO BE POPULAR, Meg Cabot has taken the typical high school teen angst and mixed it up with an all-too-believable situation to create a wonderful, fast-paced read. I'd recommend this book to all fans of Ms. Cabot, all fans of contemporary stories, all fans of young adult literature, period. This is another winner from the queen of teen fiction. Trust me. Pick up a copy of HOW TO BE POPULAR, and you won't be disappointed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4724800627174710449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

But this year is 11th grade and she is tired of the 5 years that Lauren has held the grudge. And this year she has an advantage, a book on how to be popular. A book about unknown love and unexpected experiences, Meg Cabot does it again! <div id="review_168275983" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168275983" />
    <a title="Bethany Huang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3894583-bethany-huang"><img alt="Bethany Huang" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442521188p2/3894583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168275983?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bethany Huang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bethany Huang" href="/user/show/3894583-bethany-huang">Bethany Huang</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6571586-how-to-be-popular">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168275983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7818577350796318394">OMG!!!! I just really have to say that this book is completely amazing. Meg Cabot sums up every girl's (or maybe...um, boys?) dreams of being popular-and the real reality. It is pretty hard to make normal school life sound interesting unless you're writing something paranormal, like angels, vampires or the like (trust me, I've seen almost all of the variations you can possibly get.). <br/><br/>"Crazytop" (courtesy of Jason, here) aka Steph Landry is known for the saying, "way to pull a Steph Landry,". Tha</span>
  <span id="freeText7818577350796318394" style="display:none">OMG!!!! I just really have to say that this book is completely amazing. Meg Cabot sums up every girl's (or maybe...um, boys?) dreams of being popular-and the real reality. It is pretty hard to make normal school life sound interesting unless you're writing something paranormal, like angels, vampires or the like (trust me, I've seen almost all of the variations you can possibly get.). <br /><br />"Crazytop" (courtesy of Jason, here) aka Steph Landry is known for the saying, "way to pull a Steph Landry,". That's Lauren's way of payback-by the way, she's the most popular girl in school. Steph spilled Super Big RedGulp (it stains-and when I say stains, I mean really stains!) all over her five years from the present, and to that day, Lauren still holds a grudge. Just to make it more complicated, Steph is almost obsessed with Mark Finley, Lauren's somewhat phony and clueless but nice boyfriend.<br /><br />Meg Cabot has really outdone herself this time. I think that this was even better than the Princess Diaries-wait, I know so. And I think the rest of the nation agrees with me- the Princess Diaries is a New York Times bestseller, but this book is National. Steph, that's really a way to pull a Steph Landry! :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="7818577350796318394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035015002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5326978668975994440">To see full review click <a href='https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/08/25/obviously-they-forgot-the-disclaimerhow-to-be-popular-by-meg-cabot/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>Meg Cabot was like one of my role models growing up. Which is a pretty difficult tasks to do considering the other woman on that list (note to self: one day publish said list on my blog). However, as extraordinary as some of her books are, there are some that aren’t so good.<br/><br/>And now that I’m older and more cynical (thanks to reading five thousand YA books-well, probably less than that but it feels like that much) and the market has grown,well, this book really sucks.</span>
  <span id="freeText5326978668975994440" style="display:none">To see full review click <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/08/25/obviously-they-forgot-the-disclaimerhow-to-be-popular-by-meg-cabot/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />Meg Cabot was like one of my role models growing up. Which is a pretty difficult tasks to do considering the other woman on that list (note to self: one day publish said list on my blog). However, as extraordinary as some of her books are, there are some that aren’t so good.<br /><br />And now that I’m older and more cynical (thanks to reading five thousand YA books-well, probably less than that but it feels like that much) and the market has grown,well, this book really sucks.<br /><br />I hate to say it, but it does.<br /><br />Have I really changed that much as a reader?<br /><br />Probably yes and no. My thoughts of the book originally were meh. I wasn’t that impressed, but upon reread I was just shocked at how bland and insipid it was. And that this book came from the Meg Cabot.<br /><br />The story itself is simple but decent. Simplicity can be a good thing though, some of my favorite contemporary romances are simple. But at times, How to be Popular felt too cookie cutter. Every single aspect of the plot was predictable and the Cabot tropes were all there.<br /><br />Nothing out there at all. And I could’ve totally gotten that if the characters felt a little bit more realistic.<br /><br />Realistic and likable.<br /><br />Because it took me more than a little time to warm up to Steph.<br /><br />Dare I say, I don’t like her.<br /><br />Yes, I’m going to say it. I do not like Steph Landry and I totally understand why people were making fun of her for all those years-stupid Big Gulp aside.<br /><br />Do you really you think it’s perfectly okay to play peeping Tom on your best friend and then crush on another guy while constantly slut slamming anyone who might look a little bit better than you?<br /><br />Really?<br /><br />Throughout reading this my head I kept thinking, is this really from the same woman who created Michael Moscovitz, Mia Thermopolis, Suze Simon, and Jesse de Silva.<br /><br />Well, the book cover says it is.<br /><br />But the book felt so phoned in, guys. Steph and Jason there were some cute moments…but as far as the panty melting scenes that you see in other Meg books.<br /><br />Not there.<br /><br />I almost felt like Jason was some prize given to Steph at the end for making good life choices.<br /><br />Dumb.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5326978668975994440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_605288404" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605288404" />
    <a title="Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6665735-books"><img alt="Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419956881p2/6665735.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605288404?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Books" href="/user/show/6665735-books">Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330444064" href="/book/show/1924014.How_to_Be_Popular">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6665735-books?shelf=reviewed-2013">reviewed-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605288404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16597712094371532575">I think this is a great book for every person to read, no matter what your age. The story is focused on Stephanie Landry wanting to be part of the popular crowd mainly because she’s in love with quarterback Mark Finley, the most popular student at Steph’s school. It doesn’t take long for Steph, an ordinary girl, to take matters into her hands and with the help of a book on how to be popular which she got in a box of old books from her best friend Jason’s grandmother, and some money she borrowed </span>
  <span id="freeText16597712094371532575" style="display:none">I think this is a great book for every person to read, no matter what your age. The story is focused on Stephanie Landry wanting to be part of the popular crowd mainly because she’s in love with quarterback Mark Finley, the most popular student at Steph’s school. It doesn’t take long for Steph, an ordinary girl, to take matters into her hands and with the help of a book on how to be popular which she got in a box of old books from her best friend Jason’s grandmother, and some money she borrowed from her grandfather, to gain enough self-confidence to take on the popular crowd at school and become one of them.<br /><br />Although the story centers on how to become a popular person, the message isn’t exactly that. In Steph’s quest to win Mark’s attention and fit into his crowd, although she’s hated by his girlfriend, Lauren, Steph learns a few valuable lessons. Following the advice from The Book she learns that being popular is all about having self-confidence, making people around you feel like they’re the most important person to you, the value of a genuine smile, and the importance of true friends. All the lessons she learns from The Book are ones we can apply in our daily lives, whether we want to be popular or not. Actually, it has nothing to do with popularity, but simply being the best person you can be, for yourself and to others. The most important lesson Stephanie learns at the end of the story is one The Book didn’t teach her but which experience did - that being popular isn’t all it’s cut out to be. <br /><br />I enjoyed the characters and their background stories, and I liked that each of them came from such interesting, somewhat dysfunctional families. Mean girl, Lauren, is rather stereotypical of mean girls portrayed in other YA books and movies, but the rest of the characters were all authentic with quirky, endearing traits. There’s really nothing new to this story than what I’ve read before, but still I enjoyed it for the positive message it sends to young girls without being too in your face about it. Lots of laughs throughout the book and an ending that leaves you smiling gets this book an easy five stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16597712094371532575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14862505463341880294" style="display:none"> Meg Cabot’s How To Be Popular was a butt kicking great. She gives a theme to every book she writes. This is why I love Cabot’s writing style. I can also relate to the characters in the story somewhat. Thats why this book was great<br /><br /> This book has shown me a great theme. Popularity is a piece of crap. Well, really popularity is the easiest thing to gain but hardest to hold. What they saying is that popularity has it”s snares and no benefit for them. So this book showed me that people will accept you the way you are.<br /><br /> I love Cabot’s style of writing. She makes all her books girly and fun. Meg Cabot books usually teaches us a lesson about how to get through in life. Cabot writing usually makes it understandable to “young teens and uses the grammar we may use. So her books makes good way to understand.<br /><br /> The characters in the book was fun to read about. The main character, Steph Landry, got on my nerves because she wanted to be popular and started changing her look and hung out with the populars. My least favorite character was Lauren because she’s mean and started the “Don’t pull a Steph Landry’ phrase after an incident around 6th grade. Cabot makes me believe in them as people because the book is realistic fiction so this could happen in real life. That’s why I love Cabot’s characters.<br /><br /> This is why I love this book. It tells us a great theme about popularity. I like Meg Cabot’s style of writing and the characters. I would love for people to read this book so much. So, yeah read this book.</span>

<div id="review_65207047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65207047" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2347498-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243137714p2/2347498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65207047?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/2347498-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2347498-laura?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65207047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9593691953542623463">I actually read this a few months ago and promptly forgot everything about it. How To Be Popular is a standard, disposable piece of YA fluff. It’s simple, it’s quick, and overall, it’s enjoyable if you have no expectations of reading something fantastic (or even memorable, in this case).<br/><br/>How To Be Popular is about Steph Landry, an average, yet lovable highschooler in a small town. Although she is far from friendless, she is not at all popular, mostly due to an embarrassing junior high school inci</span>
  <span id="freeText9593691953542623463" style="display:none">I actually read this a few months ago and promptly forgot everything about it. How To Be Popular is a standard, disposable piece of YA fluff. It’s simple, it’s quick, and overall, it’s enjoyable if you have no expectations of reading something fantastic (or even memorable, in this case).<br /><br />How To Be Popular is about Steph Landry, an average, yet lovable highschooler in a small town. Although she is far from friendless, she is not at all popular, mostly due to an embarrassing junior high school incident that the queen bee of the school will never let Steph live down. Basically, the story revolves around Steph, who finds a self help book about how to be popular, trying to change her status while facing a few other friend and family situations.<br /><br />There’s nothing special abotu How To Be Popular, yet it is exactly what it should be–fun, light-hearted, and sugary. The characters in this book are nice teenagers with nice, easy to solve problems, which is why I think it would be a good tween book (as opposed to full on teens, who would probably snicker at poor little Steph and her popularity problems). Readers looking for substance should go elsewhere, but for readers seeking tween fluff, How To Be Popular will fit the bill.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9593691953542623463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_28329986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28329986" />
    <a title="Namratha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114559-namratha"><img alt="Namratha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406702134p2/114559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28329986?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Namratha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Namratha" href="/user/show/114559-namratha">Namratha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330444064" href="/book/show/1924014.How_to_Be_Popular">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=journey-within">journey-within</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28329986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10129239030059846073"><b>
  <i>‘Way to pull a Steph Landry’</i>
</b><br/><br/>…and that cruel taunt has been burning <b>Steph Landry</b>’s ears since the time that she was a clumsy twelve-year old who accidentally upended a Red Super Big-Gulp on Lauren Moffat’s white denim D & G skirt. And although Steph bought Lauren a brand new skirt…prima-donna hag-<i>extraordinaire</i> Lauren has never let Steph or the rest of Bloomville High School ever let the unfortunate memory fade. Ergo, whenever anyone commits a faux-pas or does something remotely dorky, it’s <i>‘</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10129239030059846073" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘Way to pull a Steph Landry’</i>
</b><br /><br />…and that cruel taunt has been burning <b>Steph Landry</b>’s ears since the time that she was a clumsy twelve-year old who accidentally upended a Red Super Big-Gulp on Lauren Moffat’s white denim D &amp; G skirt. And although Steph bought Lauren a brand new skirt…prima-donna hag-<i>extraordinaire</i> Lauren has never let Steph or the rest of Bloomville High School ever let the unfortunate memory fade. Ergo, whenever anyone commits a faux-pas or does something remotely dorky, it’s <i>‘Don’t pull a Steph’</i> or <i>‘That’s so Steph’</i> or <i>‘Don’t be such a Steph’</i> or the ever popular <i>
  <b>‘Way to pull a Steph Landry’</b>
</i>.<br /><br />But now, after five years of fading into the background and being content with mocking the in-crowd from afar with fellow rejects <b>Jason</b> and <b>Becca</b>…Steph is ready for a change. She has laid her hands on a book titled <u>‘How-To-Be-Popular’</u> and is ready to implement all the guidelines that the author has cheerfully spelt out. So, it’s a new hairstyle, a spanking new (<i>yet, tastefully put together</i>) wardrobe and a sociable personality. She’s ready to grab the eyeballs of the popular kids with her new assertiveness. No more wallflower-impersonation. Steph Landry is ready to shine and dazzle and poke-one-in-the-eye of uber-witch - Lauren Moffat and attract the attention of handsome quarterback - Mike Finley.<br /><br />But in the quest for fitting-in, she’s in danger of alienating her best friends; Jason (<i>who interestingly enough has gotten taller and noticeably hotter</i>) and Becca (<i>who has never really left behind her scared-witless, farmgirl-in-a-new-setting persona</i>). Does getting a shoe-in into the elite pack mean compromising on things that Steph strongly believes in? Does it mean hurting the people who have always stood by her through the rough patches? <br /><br /><br /><b>Meg Cabot</b> is the literary equivalent of comfort-food. Her books are frothy, funny and wholly enjoyable. Her heroines are gutsy teenagers. While they are generally practical individuals, all of them have occasional spasms of self-doubt and flashes of insecurity to keep them real. Cabot also manages to deal with teen-issues with her usual brand of sparky dialogue and a down-to-earth approach. <br /><br /><b>How To Be Popular</b> is a fun read. It has a likeable, non-whiney heroine in Steph and a cast of oddball characters who while they might be a tad predictable are still engaging. Don’t let the title put you off. It’s not…I repeat…NOT….a self-help book. What it is, is another of Cabot’s sassy yet serious takes on the quintessential teen girl.</span>

          </span>

</b><br /><br /><b>3.5 of 5 stars (Please read my rating system further below). </b> <i>How to Be Popular</i> was the first book by Meg Cabot that I ever read. I thought it was very cute and fast paced. The characters!; <b>Oh how I loved them</b>! Meg Cabot adds such quirky and lovable traits to all of her characters (Steph, Jason, and the Grandpa especially), and I definitely became emotionally attached to a majority of them. I also really liked Steph's character development. Being able to experience her journey so vividly made me like the book even more! Overall, I definitely recommend you pick this up if you are in the mood for reading an adorable and quick contemporary!<br /><br /><b>My rating system</b>: (I <b>do</b> use half stars.)<br /><b>5</b> - <b>I do not use the 5 star</b>. <div id="review_1650714884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650714884" />
    <a title="Lanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22024407-lanie"><img alt="Lanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208561p2/22024407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650714884?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lanie" href="/user/show/22024407-lanie">Lanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of chick lit &amp; the movie &quot;mean girls&quot;</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=crappy-main-characters">crappy-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=stand-alone-novels">stand-alone-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650714884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10913435760789435903">2.5 stars, but rounding up since I really liked Jason & becca. & fond childhood memories. My preteen self really enjoyed this book way back when, so I'm sure other Tweens would probably enjoy it. <br/><br/>Plus, the whole thing reminds me of "mean girls" one of the few comedy movies I actually like. <br/><br/>There is one major flaw with the book though. & that is... Stephanie Landry, our protagonist. She is a judgmental bitch. Maybe not quite as bad as Zoey Redbirds, but still plenty enough of an ass to drag my ra</span>
  <span id="freeText10913435760789435903" style="display:none">2.5 stars, but rounding up since I really liked Jason &amp; becca. &amp; fond childhood memories. My preteen self really enjoyed this book way back when, so I'm sure other Tweens would probably enjoy it. <br /><br />Plus, the whole thing reminds me of "mean girls" one of the few comedy movies I actually like. <br /><br />There is one major flaw with the book though. &amp; that is... Stephanie Landry, our protagonist. She is a judgmental bitch. Maybe not quite as bad as Zoey Redbirds, but still plenty enough of an ass to drag my rating down. <br /><br />"Popular girls never tease or mock other girls" according to The Book that Steph read to help her become popular. <br /><br />Good advice.<br /><br />-_- <br /><br />except for the fact that her entire inner monologue is nothing BUT her mocking other girls. She's a jerk. Plain and simple. A nasty, judging, slut-shamming, whining, spying, i-am-better-than-everyone jerk who doesn't see good things or people even when they're standing in front of her. <br /><br />BUT! Aside from how much I HATED Steph, I did enjoy the book. The writing was decent &amp; I did like Jason. A few parts were pretty funny. It was a fun, easy read. It'd be a good pick if you like Chick lit &amp; fluffy teen romance type books. It feels like a definite happy sunny day at the beach type read. Not challenging or mind blowing, but fun. <br /><br />I'll have to look for more of Meg cabot's books. :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="10913435760789435903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_166224565" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166224565" />
    <a title="Sabrina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536114-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425694026p2/3536114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina " href="/user/show/3536114-sabrina">Sabrina </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People with low/no expectations. Little girls.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166224565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6042429861991174682"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703469.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is how I felt during the majority of the book. It was just so bland and monotone that I did not laugh a single time during the whole time I read the book.<br/><br/>Not a single time.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703470.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is important mainly because being a huge fan of Meg Cabot, I expected <i>way</i> more from her. But I honestly think this is one of her weaker books (but not as weak as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9397967.Abandon__Abandon_Trilogy___1_' title='Abandon (Abandon Trilogy, #1) by Meg Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Abandon</a>, that was just horrid). <br/><br/>I really hated that main character, Steph. She was annoying and whiny and overall, a real self-centered brat. For whatever r</span>
  <span id="freeText6042429861991174682" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703469.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is how I felt during the majority of the book. It was just so bland and monotone that I did not laugh a single time during the whole time I read the book.<br><br>Not a single time.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703470.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is important mainly because being a huge fan of Meg Cabot, I expected <i>way</i> more from her. But I honestly think this is one of her weaker books (but not as weak as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9397967.Abandon__Abandon_Trilogy___1_" title="Abandon (Abandon Trilogy, #1) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Abandon</a>, that was just horrid). <br><br>I really hated that main character, Steph. She was annoying and whiny and overall, a real self-centered brat. For whatever reason, she wanted to be popular and "suddenly" she finds this book which is, wait for it, a guide on How to Be Popular.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703471.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She decides to follow the book and in the process, loses her friends and yet she still wants to be popular. The antagonist in the novel, Miss Queen Bee of the school, still embarrasses Steph about an incident that happened back in junior high. Seriously?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703472.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm sorry but with the ways these girls acted, they might as well go back to elementary school. I go to high school, it is nothing like how Meg Cabot portayed it.<br><br>Meg Cabot used the typical stereotypes of high school (popularity conquers) and rather than being more original, decides to write a book about a girl learning about popularity. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703473.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only character I found myself liking was Jason. He had that typical male lead charisma that I always find myself being drawn to. He was sweet and well, Steph doesn't deserve a guy like that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703474.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The message in this book was loud and clear: Popularity isn't worth it. I'll admit, this is a pretty important message so you know what? So long as this message is influencing young girls, I have some appreciation for this book. If it makes even just one girl more confident about herself, despite her place on the social hierarchy, then Meg Cabot did well.<br><br>But for me, it was boring. I find it easier to enjoy the moral of the story if the story is, well, enjoyable. And it wasn't.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703475.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would have rated the book higher if not for the ending. Where of course, spoiler alert, everything goes Steph's way. It all works out. Happily ever after. Blahblahblah ... no. That's not how life is, it's not how life will ever be. Life doesn't give you the perfect sugar-coated happy endings that Meg Cabot gave me. Her ending was so sugary sweet it probably had 5000 calories in it alone. Gross.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703476.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It was a quick and simple read. I don't think it should be classified as a young adult novel. Reads more like a pre-adolecent book, for girls entering high school. Boring for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349480ra/703477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Just go read the Princess Diaries series. Much better than this.<br><br><b>Overall: 1 star for sharing a good message to impressionable young girls. 1 star for Jason, the only character I liked.</b></span>

<div id="review_1638408909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5047019-spencer?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638408909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13235578202002670659"><b>
  <u>2020</u>
</b><br/>Steph is a really good main character; mostly because she makes me think of myself from high school. I was super far removed from the popular crowd, and even though I could tell they were a bunch of jerks and bitches, there was nothing I wanted more than to be accepted into their group. Steph makes the same mistake in wanting to be popular, but she takes it a step further than I did. She found herself a "get popular" book and started following it step by step. And, to be fair, it worked </span>
  <span id="freeText13235578202002670659" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>2020</u>
</b><br />Steph is a really good main character; mostly because she makes me think of myself from high school. I was super far removed from the popular crowd, and even though I could tell they were a bunch of jerks and bitches, there was nothing I wanted more than to be accepted into their group. Steph makes the same mistake in wanting to be popular, but she takes it a step further than I did. She found herself a "get popular" book and started following it step by step. And, to be fair, it worked out pretty well for her, in the end.<br /><br />I love her friendship with Becca and Jason, too, because it's such a great, pure friend group. Of course, she has to deal with the drama of Becca liking Jason. And Jason not liking Becca back (you know, in that way). But she does her best to navigate the complexities of friendship and relationships while juggling her way through her attempts to become popular.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>2019</u>
</b><br />Steph is our leading lady in this book. She's had a previous run-in in the last with a popular girl, Lauren. And Lauren has never let anyone forget about it, which is what inspires Steph to try and become a more popular girl at school. Now, this I totally get. Everyone (basically) has something in the past that they not only want to forget but also maybe want to improve how their life is. Steph is a truly likable character because she's down to earth, funny, and normal. She acts just like a normal high school girl. And she's a little bit clueless, but sweet.<br /><br />Jason is the adorable boy next door (literally) who is Steph's best friend and basically the only person who calls her on her BS when she goes a little overboard on the trying to get popular train. <br /><br />Lauren is the popular girl we all love to hate. She has the hottest boyfriend in school. She's only friends with the other popular girls in school. And she loves to pick on the kids that aren't in great social standing. And, luckily for her, Steph is a much nicer person than I am.<br /><br />Honestly a super cute story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13235578202002670659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText17464559996090825268" style="display:none">All Steph wants is to be popular. Ever since 6th grade when she accidentally spilled a giant red gulp on her super popular friend Lauren, life has been miserable. Lauren even coined the term “don’t pull a Steph” to make sure that no one ever forgot. Steph reads a book that tells her how to be popular. She buys new clothes, spends lots of time doing her hair and voices her opinion to get the A-list kids to notice her. And they do. Steph wants to make the head-hancho popular guy, Mark, fall in love with her, but realizes in the end that she’s been in love with her best friend the whole time and that Mark isn’t as great as she had previously thought. <br /><br />Despite my reservations about this book (it just seemed so awfully predictable) as I was reading the ending I couldn’t help but smile. Oh, who am I kidding? I was grinning like a crazy fool. It was just so cute! Cabot has an amiable and light hearted voice that will entertain the reader throughout the novel.</span>

  <span id="freeText5347623699962692344" style="display:none">"How to be Popular" is a childhood favorite of mine. It's sweet. It's funny. Has some fun leads. It has a decent message for tweens/teenagers, and it has a super cheesy, teen-movie type ending that I adore. <br /><br />Seriously, I do think this would make a really fun movie. Like maybe something for Netflix or Disney+? <br /><br />I really like it. It's a comfort book for me. You know the sort, I mean. One of those books you can read over and over again and still love it? The sort of book you read when you're feeling down or in a reading slump, and it perks you up. For me, its "How to be Popular" or "The Books of Elsewhere" series by Jacquline West. <br /><br />Highly recommended for fans of young adult contemporary books. :D<br /><br />My only complaint is how downplayed the main character's spying is. She REALLY shouldn't be doing that, and its really annoying how it's used as something funny. Double Standards right there. </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30679152-melissa-just-really-loves-musicals?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer937365687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer707965891895445100">I read this book a number of times as a pre-teen. Meg Cabot was my go-to author. It was super fun and I don't have much to say other than that. It is about an unpopular high schooler named Steph, who finds a book titled How To Be Popular, and uses it to try to climb her schools social ladder and become one of the popular people. But obviously, shenanigans ensue, and she realizes popularity isn't all it's made out to be. I've always wanted more from this book. Steph and Jason are some of my favou</span>
  <span id="freeText707965891895445100" style="display:none">I read this book a number of times as a pre-teen. Meg Cabot was my go-to author. It was super fun and I don't have much to say other than that. It is about an unpopular high schooler named Steph, who finds a book titled How To Be Popular, and uses it to try to climb her schools social ladder and become one of the popular people. But obviously, shenanigans ensue, and she realizes popularity isn't all it's made out to be. I've always wanted more from this book. Steph and Jason are some of my favourite Meg characters, second only to Suze and Jesse from the Mediator series. I would definitely read another book of these characters if one were ever written. It's fun, it's light, it's a quick read and I ate these sort of books up as a young 11-13 year old, so the nostalgia is huge for me. Even as a soon to be 22 year old now, I still loved it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="707965891895445100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_87096314" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87096314" />
    <a title="Jamaica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3212581-jamaica"><img alt="Jamaica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264726920p2/3212581.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87096314?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamaica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamaica" href="/user/show/3212581-jamaica">Jamaica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3212581-jamaica?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87096314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5127223540376693986">Page 1:<br/>Popular: adj. Widely liked or appreciated; liked by many acquantances; sought after for company.<br/><br/>Popularity.<br/>We all want it. Why? Because being pouplar means being liked. Everyone wants to be liked.<br/>Sadly, however, not all of us are.<br/><br/>So what do pouplar people have in common that makes them all so popular?<br/><br/>They all have:<br/>*A friendly way about them.<br/>*An eagerness to pitch in and help get the job done.<br/>*An interest in everythign that goes on at work or school.<br/>*A look that's fresh and neat.<br/><br/>These aren</span>
  <span id="freeText5127223540376693986" style="display:none">Page 1:<br />Popular: adj. Widely liked or appreciated; liked by many acquantances; sought after for company.<br /><br />Popularity.<br />We all want it. Why? Because being pouplar means being liked. Everyone wants to be liked.<br />Sadly, however, not all of us are.<br /><br />So what do pouplar people have in common that makes them all so popular?<br /><br />They all have:<br />*A friendly way about them.<br />*An eagerness to pitch in and help get the job done.<br />*An interest in everythign that goes on at work or school.<br />*A look that's fresh and neat.<br /><br />These aren't traits popular people were born with. They've cultivated these characteristics that make them so popular... (Contrary to Popular Belief right? [no pun intended:] =P )<br /><br />~Let's begin by determining yoru popularity level~<br /><br />Steph Landy is a teenager who goes to Bloomville High, works as a cashier/slave-worker for her parent's own form of a Quick-E-Mart (Sorry, Love the Simpsons), and has to live with the fact that shie is 'unpopular', especially compared to her -once- best friend, Laruen Maffot.<br /><br />Once best friend? Why yes, 'once'. You see, due to a certain bright-red-cherry Super Big Gulp (think slurpee) involving Lauren's new-white-D&amp;G Skirt, well, to say the least, the two just haven't been friends ever since, even after Steph's deep-hearted apology. At any rate, their friendship probably wouldn't last because Lauren is popular and Steph..well..she's just Steph, and being -Steph- is a bad thing. You see, everyone witness the bright red cherry Super Big Gulp Slurpee Fiasco, and now when anyone does something remotely "crack-headed, stupid, or just all out geeky, dorky, or silly" (This all covers quite a bit now doesn't it?) everyone feels the need to remark: "Don't pull a Steph Landry" or "Don't be such a Steph" or something to that effect. If it isn't bad enough that her peers are doing it, kindergarteners and adults are shouting the same thing, and they don't even know her!<br /><br />Her entire high school career looks as if its in shambles and she will just have to get used to the fact that her life will be filled with no-party invites, constant ridicule and blame, and all-time labels of geek, dork, stupid, and "Crazy-top"-as called by her "somewhat hott" friend, Jason. Dang, she can't even get her childhood friend to notice her differently, except for the fact that he constantly points out her "huge chin, [and the:] large amount of real estate between [her:] eyes!" But what's all that matter? Jason isn't popular...just ..."somewhat hott" (and maybe attainable? compared to other guys that her out of her league, especially the "hottest guy in school: Mark Finely). Oh yeah, Jason and Mark...no contest, Mark wins hands-down [mind you this is according to Steph...not myself. Just as so long as we have that cleared =P :]<br /><br />Oh if Steph could only get Mark to notice her, but that reality looks so far from her, that is, until she finds this book titled: How to be Popular.<br /><br />Understandably, that's a lot in just the first few pages, but you get the idea. Reading through, you'll find that this book is comical, has a nice set-up that allows you to keep all the characters straight, and one that you just can't stop reading until its finished (presumably if life doesn't get in the way first). <br /><br />Neverthelss, this book is definitely a novel that many girls, and guys, can relate. I mean come on, we've all probalby dreamt at some point or another about being pouplar...and if not that, then at least we've thought about it (if we weren't 'part of that group' to begin with). And if you're still in some sort of denial of never wanting that [=P:] then at least we may have thought about trying to impress, or rather get the attention of (in a good + way) that guy/girl who's deemed "out of our league".<br /><br />Cabbot manages to master all these feelings by intertwining Steph's (and really perhaps our own) story with that to the 'tips' of the book that Steph has found (and that is also consquently in our possession...well...in yours if you go buy it at BN for like $9- trust me, it's worth the $9 plus the 10% discount if your a BN member -okay done advertising...think BN 'll give me more of a cut since I so craftily inserted that promotion there? No? ...Didnt think so...sad face...)<br /><br />Anyhoo,<br /><br />it's a read you should pick up. I mean, don't you wanna know if Steph gets the guy? Or if she becomes, oh my god - popular? (maybe I'm being a little bit of cynical smart-a but eh, you'll get used to it). Or do new relationships blossom elsewhere? And what about that-excusez mon francais- bizz-itch - Lauen Moffat- who decides to make Steph's life a living hell because of one incident!?!<br /><br />Yeah~ So I'll leave you all to it. Happy reading xD<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5127223540376693986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kPegcw05GBEe2DGC5O+AykvdfRoozFsvL0KLRq2rN7bRtLPvRf0YqSz3mC/rwEA8SzXXdq/UVeaHIs9SKJUP/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h6NkW9X3mDDp9lsAKUTYJ5PtpFvLwRzNO2H7sPlCU5fG4HfHnTOYiNvZ8q0maxjRkwUON0zZEgSTAb+kfHxr3Q==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot">About Meg Cabot</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1532640822p3/11654.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot">Meg Cabot
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14782386274195481907">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText14782386274195481907" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14782386274195481907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2610019-how-to-be-popular">Quotes from How to Be Popular</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Clearly," Jason said, "you are not doing nothing. You are most definitely doing something. What it looks like you're doing is pouring packets of sugar on Lauren Moffat's head."<br /><br />Shhh," I said. "It's snowing. But only on Lauren." I shook more sugar out of the packets. "'Merry Christmas, Mr. Potter,'" I called softly down to Lauren in my best Jimmy Stewart imitation. "'Merry Christmas, you old building and Loan.'"<br /><br />Jason started cracking up, and I had to hush him as Becca saw my sugar supply running low and hastened to hand me more packets.<br /><br />Stop laughing so loud," I said to Jason. "You'll spoil this beautiful moment for them." I sprinkled more sugar over the side of the balcony. "'Merry Christmas to all, and to all a good night.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/101127-clearly-jason-said-you-are-not-doing-nothing-you-are">146 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I think we're given multiple chances to meet multiple soulmates. Sure, you could meet a soulmate in highschool. But that doesn't mean if you don't act on it, you'll never meet anyone else. You will, just at a time that's more convenient for you.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/455614-i-think-we-re-given-multiple-chances-to-meet-multiple-soulmates">75 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
